style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:14pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:14pt;font-weight:bold;">NIKE, INC. REPORTS FISCAL </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:14pt;font-weight:bold;">2020</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:14pt;font-weight:bold;">&#32;</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:14pt;font-weight:bold;">FOURTH QUARTER</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:14pt;font-weight:bold;">&#32;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:center;font-size:14pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:14pt;font-weight:bold;">AND FULL YEAR RESULTS</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">BEAVERTON, Ore., June 25, 2020</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;- NIKE, Inc. (NYSE:NKE) today reported financial results for its fiscal </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">2020</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">fourth quarter</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;and full year ended </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">May&#160;31, 2020</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">.</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Fourth quarter reported revenues were </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$6.3 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, declining from prior year as the majority of NIKE-owned and partner stores in North America, EMEA and APLA were closed due to the COVID-19 pandemic. </font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">NIKE digital sales increased 75 percent in the fourth quarter, or 79 percent on a currency-neutral basis*, with strong double-digit increases across all geographies and was approximately 30 percent of total revenue. </font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">For the fiscal year, Greater China revenues increased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;text-transform:default;">8 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, or </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;text-transform:default;">11 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a currency-neutral basis, marking its sixth consecutive year of double-digit currency-neutral growth despite the headwinds from COVID-19 in the second half of the year. </font></div></td></tr></table><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Our fourth quarter results were significantly impacted by physical store closures across North America, EMEA and APLA, where 90 percent of NIKE-owned stores were closed for roughly eight weeks in the quarter to protect the health and safety of teammates and consumers and help slow the spread of the COVID-19 pandemic. Our wholesale partners largely followed the same pattern and as a result, product shipments to wholesale customers were down nearly 50 percent resulting in lower total revenue and higher inventory. During the widespread physical store closures, we accelerated our connection and engagement with our consumers leveraging the strength of our digital ecosystem.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#8220;In a highly dynamic environment, the NIKE Brand continues to resonate strongly with consumers all over the world as our digital business accelerates in every market,&#8221; said John Donahoe, President and Chief Executive Officer, NIKE, Inc. &#8220;We are uniquely positioned to grow, and now is the time to build on NIKE's strengths and distinct capabilities. We are continuing to invest in our biggest opportunities, including a more connected digital marketplace, to extend our leadership and fuel long-term growth.&#8221;**</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">COVID-19 Update on Operations</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">As of today, approximately 90 percent of NIKE-owned stores are open across the globe. Retail traffic continues to improve week-over-week with higher conversion rates as compared to the prior year.**</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">In Greater China, nearly 100 percent of NIKE-owned stores are open. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">In North America, EMEA and APLA, approximately 90 percent of physical owned stores were closed during the fourth quarter with stores gradually reopening at different paces in each country beginning in mid-May. Today, roughly 85 percent of NIKE-owned stores are open in North America and about 90 percent in EMEA, with approximately 65 percent open in APLA or operating under reduced hours.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;&#8220;As physical retail re-opens, NIKE's strong digital trends continue, a testament to the strength of our brand and the investments we've made to elevate digital consumer experiences,&#8221; said Matt Friend, Executive Vice President and Chief Financial Officer, NIKE, Inc. &#8220;Amid macroeconomic uncertainty, we will continue to operate with agility, focused on optimizing marketplace supply and demand, cost management and leveraging our financial strength to drive long-term sustainable, profitable growth</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">.</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#8221;**</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">As we continue to reopen retail stores and increase distribution center activity, we remain focused on prioritizing the health of our teammates and consumers and have taken proactive steps to help ensure a safe environment. During the quarter, we made significant investments to provide employee pay continuity and committed over $25 million to support communities impacted by COVID-19 among other COVID-19 response efforts.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">Fourth Quarter</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">&#32;Income Statement Review</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Revenues</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">&#32;</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">for NIKE, Inc. decreased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">38 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$6.3 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, down </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">36 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a currency-neutral basis, primarily due to owned and partner physical store closures across North America, EMEA and APL A due to COVID-19, partially offset by growth in Greater China.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Gross margin</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;decreased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">820 basis points</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">37.3 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;as higher full-price average selling prices, despite increased wholesale discounts, were more than offset by higher product costs including factory cancellation charges, increased inventory obsolescence reserves and the adverse rate impact of supply chain fixed costs on lower wholesale shipments primarily due to COVID-19.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Selling and administrative expense</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;decreased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">6 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$3.2 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, which included an incremental $178 million increase in bad debt expense. Demand creation expense was </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$823 million</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, down </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">19 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to prior year as retail and brand marketing spend was shifted as sporting events were canceled or delayed due to COVID-19. Operating overhead expense decreased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">1 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$2.4 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;driven primarily by lower total wages and travel and related expenses, partially offset by higher bad debt expense. </font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">The </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">effective tax rate</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;was </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">1.7 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, compared to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">20.4 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;for the same period last year. This is primarily due to the mix of earnings taxed in the U</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:11pt;">.</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">S. and favorability attributable to items such as the use of foreign tax credits.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Net loss</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;was </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$790 million</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;and </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">diluted net loss per share</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;was </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$0.51</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;driven by lower revenue and gross margin as a result of the COVID-19 impact on operations, partially offset by lower selling and administrative expenses. </font></div></td></tr></table><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">Fiscal </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">2020</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">&#32;Income Statement Review</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Revenues</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-weight:bold;">&#32;</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">for NIKE, Inc. fell </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">4 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$37.4 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, down </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">2 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a currency-neutral basis due to the impact of COVID-19 on business operations, primarily in the fourth quarter. In the first half of fiscal 2020, prior to COVID-19, NIKE, Inc. revenue was up 9 percent, or 11 percent on a currency-neutral basis, reflecting strong, broad-based consumer demand, higher full-price sales realization and a double-digit increase in digital sales.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#9702;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">In fiscal 2020, digital sales increased 47 percent, or 49 percent on a currency-neutral basis, with all geographies growing strong double-digits.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#9702;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">Greater China revenues increased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">8 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, or </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">11 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;on a currency-neutral basis, marking its sixth consecutive year of double-digit growth on a currency-neutral basis.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Gross margin</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;decreased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">130 basis points</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">43.4 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;as higher full-price average selling prices, despite higher discounts due to COVID-19, were more than offset by higher product costs including tariffs in the U.S., as well as factory cancellation charges, increased inventory obsolescence reserves and the adverse rate impact of supply chain cost on a lower volume of wholesale shipments in the fourth quarter.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:24px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:11pt;padding-left:0px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:11pt;"><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold;">Selling and administrative expense</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;increased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">3 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$13.1 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">. Demand creation expense was </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$3.6 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">, down </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">4 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to prior year primarily due to lower retail, brand and sports marketing expenses as sporting events were postponed or canceled and a majority of physical stores were closed globally during the fourth quarter. Operating overhead expense increased </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">7 percent</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;to </font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">$9.5 billion</font><font style="font-family:Arial;font-size:11pt;">&#32;driven primarily by higher wage-related expenses to support our continued investments in end-to-end digital capabilities and higher bad debt expense, partially offset by lower travel and related spend.</font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0"
